## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillators / dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t, which is the standard second-order ODE form for (non)linear harmonic oscillators. Typical structures combine restoring forces in x (often odd nonlinearities), damping/friction in v (linear or nonlinear), and optional external or parametric forcing in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear damped oscillator (mass normalized): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (small oscillations with viscous damping; signs set by convention)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (conservative): dv_dt = c0 * x (restoring acceleration proportional to displacement; energy-conserving if no v term)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring + damping)
- Quintic stiffness oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (stronger amplitude-dependent frequency shift)
- Nonlinear damping (cubic damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (damping grows with speed; aero/hydrodynamic-like damping surrogate)
- Quadratic drag / turbulent damping surrogate: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (directional drag proportional to v|v|)
- Dry/Coulomb friction oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sign(v) (stick-slip/friction dominated dynamics; approximated with sign)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (self-excited oscillator with amplitude-limiting nonlinear damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator form: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (alternative self-excitation mechanism; can yield limit cycles depending on signs)
- Externally forced Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t + c5) (periodically driven nonlinear resonance/chaos)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (time-varying stiffness; Mathieu-type behavior)
- Nonlinear stiffness saturation: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 / (x**2 + c2) + c3 * v (restoring force becomes effectively bounded/softened at large |x|)
- Time-dependent damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) * v (periodic modulation of dissipation/active control)
- Piecewise-linear spring (approx.): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * Abs(x) * sign(x) + c2 * v (models stiffness change with displacement magnitude using |x|x)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: odd dependence in x (e.g., x, x**3, x + x**3) typically indicates a symmetric potential and oscillations about x=0.
- Conservative vs dissipative: absence of v terms suggests near-energy-conserving motion; inclusion of terms proportional to v, v**3, or v*Abs(v) indicates dissipation.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency: adding x**3 (Duffing) or higher odd powers yields frequency shifts with amplitude (hardening/softening depending on coefficient sign).
- Self-excited limit cycles: factors like (c - x**2) * v imply negative damping at small |x| and positive damping at large |x|, producing stable oscillation amplitudes.
- Coulomb friction signatures: sign(v) terms create non-smooth dynamics, corners in phase portraits, and near-constant-magnitude friction opposing motion.
- Velocity-squared drag: v*Abs(v) indicates drag scaling with speed squared and strong damping at high velocities with direction set by v.
- External periodic forcing: additive sin(c*t + phi) terms create resonance peaks, entrainment, and possible chaotic responses when combined with nonlinearity.
- Parametric excitation: time-multiplying x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c*t))*x) indicates stiffness modulation, leading to instability tongues (Mathieu behavior).
- State-dependent damping modulation: coefficients of v depending on x (e.g., (c - x**2)*v) often encode energy injection/removal linked to displacement.
- Saturating stiffness/nonlinearity: rational forms in x (e.g., x**3/(x**2+c)) model restoring forces that soften or cap at large displacement compared with pure polynomials.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (PO37)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - c1*beta*v - omega0**c2*(gamma*t + c3)*x
Candidate formulas: 70

GT (fixed function):
\[
0.719321236251799\sin(t)\;-\;0.0856781567252997\,v^3\;-\;1.91960248272986\,v\;-\;1.73029531320599\,x\,(0.0808213006269486\,t+1)
\]
Expand the \(x\) part:
\[
-1.73029531320599\,x\;-\;(1.73029531320599\cdot 0.0808213006269486)\,t x
\]
So GT is exactly of the form
\[
A\sin(t)+Bv^3+Cv+Dx+E(tx)
\]
with **no constant offset**, and **no other nonlinearities** (no abs, exp, log, extra trig in \(v\) or \(x\), etc.).

Compute the needed \(tx\) coefficient:
```text
E = -1.73029531320599 * 0.0808213006269486 ≈ -0.139865 (approx)
```

Thus any candidate can match iff it can be reduced (by setting free constants) to:
- a sine term that is exactly \(\sin(t)\) up to amplitude (phase allowed but must still equal \(\sin(t)\) for all \(t\)),
- linear \(x\),
- linear \(t x\),
- linear \(v\),
- cubic \(v^3\),
- and all extra terms must be zeroed out.

Below, for each candidate, I check whether it contains exactly these building blocks and whether all extra terms can be eliminated by setting some constants to 0, and whether the sine can be made \(\sin(t)\) (via frequency/phase choices).

---

### 1. `... + c8*v*exp(c9*t)`
Has extra \(v e^{c9 t}\) term. Can set \(c8=0\) to remove. Remaining terms include \(x\), constant, \(\sin(c3+c4 t)\), \(v^3\), \(v\), \(t x\). Set constant \(c1=0\). Sine: choose \(c4=1\), \(c3=0\) to get \(\sin(t)\). Then choose coefficients to match GT. **Match possible.**

### 2. `... + c7*v*sin(c8*t + c9)`
Extra \(v\sin(\cdot)\) term; set \(c7=0\). Remaining has \(x\), \(\sin(c2+c3 t)\), \(v\), \(t x\), \(v^3\). Choose \(c3=1,c2=0\) for \(\sin(t)\). Set coefficients to GT. **Match possible.**

### 3. `... + c7*v*(c8 + t)**c9`
Extra \(v(t+c8)^{c9}\); set \(c7=0\). Remaining matches needed basis. **Match possible.**

### 4. `... + c6*x*cos(c7*t)`
Extra \(x\cos(c7 t)\) term; set \(c6=0\). Remaining has \(x\), \(\sin\), \(v\), \(t x\), \(v^3\). **Match possible.**

### 5. `... + c5*exp(c6*t)`
Extra \(e^{c6 t}\); set \(c5=0\). Also has constant \(c1\) which must be 0. Remaining matches basis. **Match possible.**

### 6. `... + c8*x*Abs(x)`
Extra \(x|x|\) (not removable by identity). Set \(c8=0\). Then same as (1) without exp term; set \(c1=0\). **Match possible.**

### 7. `... + c4*sin(c5*x + c6)`
Extra \(\sin(\text{affine in }x)\); set \(c4=0\). Remaining has \(x\), \(\sin(t)\)-type, \(v\), \(t x\), \(v^3\). **Match possible.**

### 8. `... + c5*v**c6 + ... + c9*x*Abs(x)**2`
Extra \(x|x|^2 = x^3\) (since \(|x|^2=x^2\)), so it’s \(c9 x^3\); set \(c9=0\). Also \(v^{c6}\) can be made \(v^3\) by \(c6=3\), but GT needs both \(v^3\) and \(v\); candidate already has separate \(c7 v\). Set constant \(c1=0\). Sine adjustable. **Match possible.**

### 9. `... + c8*x**3`
Extra \(x^3\); set \(c8=0\). Then matches basis (with constant term present; set \(c1=0\)). **Match possible.**

### 10. `... + c7*x*Abs(x)**2`
That term is \(c7 x^3\); set \(c7=0\). Remaining matches basis; set constant \(c1=0\). **Match possible.**

### 11. `... + c7*x*exp(c8*t)`
Extra \(x e^{c8 t}\); set \(c7=0\). Remaining matches basis. **Match possible.**

### 12. `... + c7*x*(c8 + t)**c9`
Extra \(x(t+c8)^{c9}\); set \(c7=0\). Remaining matches basis. **Match possible.**

### 13. `... + c7*x**3/(x**2 + 1)`

### 14. `... + c8*x**5`

### 15. `... + c5*x**c6`
